Re: Our Client: Charles Johnson Your Insured: Robert Lowe Date of Incident: April 18, 2023 Claim No.: 1748L638H

The following is a settlement demand on behalf of our client, Charles Johnson (“Mr. Johnson” or “our client”), for the injuries he sustained on April 18, 2023, when Mr. Johnson was injured in an incident involving Robert Lowe (“Mr. Lowe” or “your insured’’).

This demand is prepared in an attempt to resolve our client’s claim and is a privileged settlement communication under K.R.E. 408. This demand is not intended for use in future litigation without our consent. No information contained herein should be considered a factual or legal admission by our client.

We expect that you will provide us with a list of any additional items you need to fully evaluate this demand within 15 days of the date of this letter. We will respond to any requests you make for additional information forthwith. We also ask that this demand be immediately forwarded to all insurance company decision-makers and, of course, the insured policyholder.

1. FACTS & LIABILITY




On April 18, 2023, Mr. Johnson was the restrained driver of a vehicle (“Unit 2”) traveling westbound on Main Street in Louisville, Jefferson County, Kentucky. At the same time, Mr. Lowe was the driver of a vehicle (“Unit 1”) traveling southbound on 22nd Street. Eugene Kalagin’s vehicle (“Unit 3”) was parked in a parking lot. On the date of the incident, Mr. Johnson proceeded into the intersection at Main Street and 22nd Street when, suddenly and without warning, Mr. Lowe entered the intersection directly into the path of Mr. Johnson. Due to the sudden and unexpected appearance of Mr. Lowe in the intersection, Mr. Johnson did not have time to take evasive action and struck Mr. Lowe’s vehicle, which caused a chain reaction where Mr. Lowe then struck Mr. Kalagin’s vehicle. The collision resulted in Mr. Johnson sustaining significant personal injuries and other damages.

As exposed in the Kentucky Uniform Police Traffic Collision Report, Officer Stephen Ates of the Louisville Metropolitan Police Department investigated the collision. While Officer Ates did not indicate that Mr. Lowe was responsible for the collision, it is clear from the facts and circumstances of the collision that Mr. Lowe was the sole contributor to the collision due to his failure to stop at a red light.

The conditions for establishing liability, in this case, are clear. Mr. Lowe owed a duty of care to the other drivers on the road. Pursuant to KY Rev Stat § 189.231(2), “[t]he driver of any vehicle

shall obey the instructions of any official traffic control device applicable thereto unless otherwise directed by a traffic or police officer, subject to the exceptions granted the driver of an authorized emergency vehicle.” On the date of loss, Mr. Lowe lacked attentiveness and due care and failed to obey a traffic control device. As a result of Mr. Lowe’s acts and/or omissions on April 18, 2023, Mr. Johnson suffered significant personal injuries and damages for which Mr. Lowe is undoubtedly liable.

3.3. Future Medical Expenses

Mr. Johnson continues to experience pain and symptomatology as a result of the injuries he sustained in the incident at issue and will require additional treatment moving forward, including, but not limited to, chiropractic care and an orthopedic consultation. Thus, a conservative estimate of future medical care for Mr. Johnson is $6,311.00.

3.4. Past and Future Pain and Suffering

There is no question that the April 18, 2023, incident caused Mr. Johnson a great deal of physical and emotional pain and suffering. As a result of the incident, Mr. Johnson suffered serious injuries that affected his entire life. Mr. Johnson experienced difficulty and pain when trying to complete simple daily activities that he used to be able to complete with ease prior to the April 18, 2023, incident. At this time, Mr. Johnson is still being treated for the injuries he sustained in the incident and continues to experience pain and a limited range of motion in all the involved areas.

Simply put, Mr. Johnson will be reminded of the April 18, 2023, incident every single day for the rest of his life when he awakens, when he drives in a car, when he goes to work, and when he tries to interact with friends and family or meet new people. The pain and impact of this ordeal will never leave Mr. Johnson, and this should remain at the forefront of your consideration as you evaluate Mr. Johnson’s significant non-economic damages.

The goal of compensatory damages is to make the injured party whole to the extent it is possible to measure the injury in terms of money. Ky. Cent. Ins. Co. v. Schneider, 15 S.W.3d 373, 374 (Ky. 2000). Damages should include fair compensation for any physical or mental suffering caused by the injury. Ky. Cent. Ins. Co. v. Schneider, 15 S.W.3d 373, 374 (Ky. 1995). There is no set rule for computing damages for pain and suffering. The general rule is that the damages must be reasonable, free from sentiment and free from punishment so as not to amount to punitive damages. Noel v. Creary, 385 S.W.2d 951, 953 (Ky. 1965). The probability of future pain and suffering may be considered when calculating damages if the evidence shows that future pain and suffering may stem from the injury. Nussbaum v. Caskey, 235 Ky. 640, 32 S.W.2d 18, 19 (Ky. App. 1930).

Liability is clear. Should this case go to a jury, the sole question to answer would be how much money Mr. Johnson is entitled to receive under Kentucky law.

Per Diem Analysis

Our conservative per diem analysis shows that Mr. Johnson’s claim for past, present, and future pain and suffering is valued at $60,296.00. A jury will consider not only Mr. Johnson’s initial pain and suffering to date, but also his subsequent pain and suffering. Below are some very conservative figures we would present to a jury to consider, in addition to his other damages:

e $26.00/hr. for initial pain and suffering from April 18, 2023, to June 21, 2023; and e $5.75/hr. for subsequent pain and suffering from June 21, 2023, to June 21, 2024.




Pain & Suffering

Initial Pain & Suffering

Initial Period (in Days) 64 Waking Hours/Day 16.0 Reasonable Compensation/Hour $26.00 Total Initial Pain & Suffering $26,624.00 Subsequent Pain & Suffering Subsequent Days with Pain 366 Waking Hours/Day 16.0 Reasonable Compensation/Hour $5.75 Total Subsequent Pain & Suffering $33,672.00

Total Pain and Suffering $60,296.00

In light of the per diem analysis above, we assert that $60,296.00 is fair and equitable compensation for Mr. Johnson’s initial and subsequent pain and suffering.

4. DEMAND TO SETTLE We believe that the above evaluation is a fair and reasonable calculation of our client’s damages. As you will note, our client’s economic and non-economic damages total at least $80,253.40. Our

client will settle his claim for a minimum of the policy limits of $50,000.00.

If a software product is being used to generate payout ranges as to this claim, we request that you communicate the range of results generated by your software.

Please respond within 15 days of receipt of this demand. If the terms of this demand are not accepted, we have been authorized by our client to promptly file suit. Please feel free to contact me should you have any questions.

Sincerely,

Aaron G. Whaley, Esq

Narrative

EMS dispatched for a motor vehicle accident. On arrival one patient is found sitting in drivers seat of involved vehicle. Pt is A&O x4 and able to answer all questions appropriately. Pt is able to recall events of accident and denies any loss of consciousness. Displays no signs of altered mental status. Pt is c/o traumatic thoracic pain, as well as pain to bilateral lower extremities. Pt states he was restrained, airbags did deploy and hit patient in the chest. Pt denies any head or neck pain or tenderness. Pt was up and walking prior to arrival and did not require extrication. No intrusion into passenger compartment seen. Windshield is intact. He is able to ambulate without difficulty and describes no additional pain doing so. Pt reports it is painful to take a deep breath. Lung sounds are clear and equal. Seatbelt sign is not present. Basic Information

Patient is a 71-year-old male who presents after MVA. Patient was the restrained driver in a motor vehicle accident. He reports he was traveling roughly 20 mph when another vehicle struck the back driver side of his. He denies hitting his head, loss of consciousness. He is endorsing sternal chest pain with increased pain on deep inspiration. No other extremity pain noted and denying abdominal pain.

Gen: NAD

Pulm: CTAB, Unlabored respirations

Chest xr to be completed and no other CT imaging based on no LOC, blood thinner or other concerning signs of symptoms. On reevaluation, patient had improvement of their symptoms. Patient reassured and

discharged to home with muscle relaxer and recommendations of Tylenol and ibuprofen alternating for their pain. Rturn precautions discussed and patient expresses understanding

As part of your treatment plan, your provider may have prescribed a limited course of a controlled substance. This medication may be given to help people with moderate or severe pain or for other medical conditions, but there are risks involved with treatment. Common side effects may include nausea, constipation, drowsiness, sweating, itching, dry mouth, and rash. More serious side effects may include cognitive and motor impairment, like problems with thinking, concentrating, alertness, and movement (e.g. slowed reflexes), and driving and operating heavy machinery can be dangerous. It is important for you to talk to your provider if you have these side effects or questions. These controlled substances can produce physical dependence and be habit-forming if taken for an extended period of time, which means that the body has gotten used to them and may experience withdrawal symptoms, if they are abruptly stopped. Withdrawal symptoms can include runny nose, sweating, goose bumps, diarrhea, abdominal cramping, rapid heartbeat, difficulty sleeping, and nervousness. Please dispose of unused and expired medications per pharmacy guidance.

Education Materials

Heat Therapy

Heat therapy can help ease sore, stiff, injured, and tight muscles and joints.

Heat relaxes your muscles. This may help ease your pain and muscle spasms.

What are the risks?

If you have any of the following conditions, do not use heat therapy unless your doctor says it is okay. These conditions include:

. New bruises. . Open wounds. . Any of these in the area being treated: —46 Healing wounds. —46 Infected skin. —46 Scarred skin. . Problems with how blood moves through your body (circulation). . Loss of feeling (numbness} in the part of your body that is being treated. . Unusual swelling of the part of the body that is being treated. . Blood clots. . Diabetes.

Not being able to communicate pain. This may include young children and people who have problems with their brain function

(dementia).

How to use heat therapy

There are different kinds of heat therapy. These include:

Moist heat pack. Hot water bottle. Electric heating pad. Heated gel pack. Heated wrap.

Warm water bath.

Your doctor will tell you how to use heat therapy. In general, you should:

Place a towel between your skin and the heat source. Leave the heat on for 20-30 minutes. Your skin may turn pink.

Take off the heat if your skin turns bright red. This is very important. If you cannot feel pain, heat, or cold, you have a greater risk of getting burned.

Your doctor may also tell you to take a warm water bath. To do this:

On rR woh >

Put a non-slip pad in the bathtub to prevent a fall.

Fill the bathtub with warm water.

Check the water temperature.

Soak in the water for 15-20 minutes, or as told by your doctor. Be careful when you stand up after the bath. You may feel dizzy. Pat yourself dry after the bath. Do not rub your skin to dry it.

General recommendations for heat therapy

Be careful not to burn your skin when using heat therapy. High heat or using heat for a long time can cause burns. Do not sleep while using heat therapy. Only use heat therapy while you are awake.

Check your skin during heat therapy.

Do not use heat therapy if you have a new injury, especially if you have swelling on the injured area.

. Do not use heat therapy on areas of your skin that are already irritated, such as with a rash or sunburn. . Do not use heat therapy if your skin turns bright red.

. You have blisters, redness, swelling, or loss of feeling in the area where you use heat therapy. . You have new pain. . You have pain that gets worse.

Summary

. Heat therapy is the use of heat to help ease sore, stiff, injured, and tight muscles and joints. . There are different types of heat therapy. Your doctor will tell you which one to use.

. Only use heat therapy while you are awake.

. Watch your skin to make sure you do not get burned while using heat therapy.

Cigarette Smoking

The facts are clear, cigarette smoking will shorten your life. Smoking can cause many illnesses along the way. As a healthcare provider, we recommend that you stop smoking. Assistance with quitting is available by contacting 1-800-QUIT-NOW. This is a free resource providing counseling, support, and referral. Or you may contact your personal physician.

Don't Wait! a Heart Attack Before It Star

What is a heart attack?

A heart attack is damage or death to a part of the heart from severely decreased or lack of blood flow to the heart. Over time, arteries can become narrow from the buildup of fat and cholesterol, which is called plaque. The plaque can rupture causing a blood clot to form. When the blood clot forms, the artery can become severely narrowed or completely blocked, causing a heart attack.

« Heart attack is the leading cause of death in the United States. « 85% of muscle damage occurs within the first 2 hours.

« Delay in the recognition of heart attack symptoms increases the chances of death.

Know the early symptoms of a heart attack:

Feeling of Pain that travels Nausea "fullness" in Jaw Pain down one or chest both arms . F Chest pressure, Fatiguelbeing Anxiety Back Pain squeezing, or discomfort Shortness of Sweating, ora Feeling of breath cold sweat Impending doom

There are unusual signs of heart attack, too! Women, the elderly, and diabetics may present with atypical symptoms:

+ Fainting/dizziness « Weakness

*« Confusion

Risk Factors for a Heart Attack

Some heart disease risk factors, such as age and family, cannot be changed. Others, like smoking and lack of exercise, can be changed.

Smoking High Cholesterol Blood Pressure Family History Obesity Age Gender (Males are

at higher risk) Lack of Exercise Diabetes Diet Stress Excessive Alcohol Intake

If you or someone you know is experiencing the signs and symptoms of a heart attack, DON'T DELAY. Call 9-1-1 immediately and seek help.

If someone collapses, perform CPR! Do not attempt to drive if you are having symptoms of heart attack.

Why Hands-Only CPR?

« Hands-Only CPR has been shown to be as effective as conventional CPR for cardiac arrests that occur outside of a hospital.

« Survival depends on immediately receiving CPR from someone nearby.

How do you perform Hands-Only CPR? There are two easy steps:

« 1. Call 9-1-1 if you see a teen or adult collapse

« 2. Push hard and fast in the center of the chest at a beat of 100 beats per minute

Save a life!

4 WAYS TO GET AHEAD OF SEPSI SEPSIS is a MEDICAL EMERGENCY. Time Matters!

Infections put you and your family at risk for a life-threatening condition called sepsis.

* Sepsis is the body's extreme response to an infection. It is life-threatening, and without timely treatment, sepsis can rapidly lead to tissue damage, organ failure, and death. Sepsis happens when an infection you already have-in your skin, lungs, urinary tract or somewhere else-riggers a chain reaction throughout your body.

Take good care of chronic conditions. PREVENT Talk to your doctor INFECTIONS about getting the recommended vaccines.

Wash your hands frequently. PRACTICE GOOD Keep cuts or open HYGIENE sores clean and covered until they

are healed.

Confusion or disorientation Shortness of breath High heart rate KNOW THE Fever, shivering, or SYMPTOMS feeling very cold Extreme pain or discomfort Clammy or sweaty skin

Given the limited resources, it is not meant to be a substitute for complete medical care. The follow-up provider you named will receive a copy of your records and all test reports. IT IS IMPORTANT THAT YOU SCHEDULE A FOLLOW-UP APPOINTMENT AND BE RE-EVALUATED. You should report any new complaints, symptoms, or remaining problems at that time. IT IS IMPOSSIBLE FOR THE EMERGENCY DEPARTMENT TO RECOGNIZE AND TREAT ALL ELEMENTS OF INJURY OR ILLNESS IN A SINGLE VISIT.

If you have been referred to a specialist provider, it means that we believe you may have a condition that requires the expertise of a specialist. These providers work in partnership with the hospital and have agreed to see referred patients in their office for further evaluation. KEEP IN MIND THAT THE SPECIALIST HAS HIS/HER OWN OFFICE POLICIES WHICH MAY REQUIRE PROPER INSURANCE OR PAYMENT UP FRONT BEFORE THE SPECIALIST WILL SEE YOU. It is your responsibility to call the specialist provider to make an appointment. We do not have the ability to refer patients to specialists/physicians that work with specific insurance companies.

Please be advised that all financial charges or billing practices are determined by that practice, not the hospital. If your insurance company requires that you see a specialist from their approved list, it is your responsibility to contact your insurance company to make those arrangements. It is also your responsibility to follow any other requirements of your insurance company necessary to obtain coverage for claims submitted.

AUTHORIZATION OF REPRESENTATIVE TO APPEAL

| understand that Medicare and other payers do not pay the difference in the cost between a private and semi-private room when use of a private room is not necessary for medical reasons. | hereby agree that the difference in the cost between a semi-private and private room will be my responsibility to pay if | request one at any point during my stay.

[ hereby authorize and convey to UofL Health the full extent permissible under Federal and State law and under any applicable insurance policy and/or employee health care benefit plan: (1) the right and ability to act as my Authorized Representative in connection with any claim, right, matter, or cause of action that | may have under such insurance policy and/or benefit plan; and (2) the right and ability to act as my Authorized Representative to pursue such claim, right, matter, or cause of action in connection with said insurance policy and/or benefit plan, including the right and ability to act as my Authorized Representative with respect to a benefit plan governed by the provisions of the Employee Retirement Income Security Act ("ERISA").

| also authorize UofL Health to act on my behalf to (1) obtain copies of my insurance policy or benefit plan documents from my insurer(s) or other Plan Administrator; (2) pursue appeals of adverse benefits decisions, claims for breaches of fiduciary duty under ERISA, external appeal review under Federal or State statute, administrative hearings, or legal actions to obtain payment from any payor; (3) disclose my protected health information to my insurer(s), its affiliates, any plan fiduciary, or independent review organization that may be involved in the resolution of claims, in connection with filing or appealing any claim for benefits due; and (4) receive any notices in connection with my benefit claims or appeals concerning same.

lf my admission to UofL Health is a result of a work-related injury, | hereby waive any privilege | may have with UofL Health, or other healthcare provider, and | hereby authorize these providers to provide the worker's compensation administrator any information related to my injury or to my past relevant medical history. In the event there is a dispute about the compensability of my claim or worker's compensation benefits, and if my employer is not specifically determined by a Court of the Department of Labor to be responsible for worker's compensation medical expenses for fhe condition or injury that is the basis of my admission, | agree to be personally responsible for all such expenses. | further agree that, if my worker’s compensation claim is settled with my employer on a disputed basis without a specific finding that such is compensable as a workers compensation injury, | (or my attorney, if | am represented) will withhold sufficient funds from any settlement to pay all amourits owed to UofL Health for treatment of the condition which is the basis for this admission, and | hereby grant an assignment to UofL Health for payment of all such expenses under such circumstances.

PERSONAL EQUIPMENT AND VALUABLES

| understand that UofL Health does not accept responsibility and will not reimburse me for the loss of money, jewelry, eyewear, hearing aids, dentures, clothing or other personal property or valuables | bring to UofL Health. | fake full responsibility for such Items and agree to release UofL Health from any and all liability from damage, loss or theft of such items unless, as applicable, the items are deposited at UofL Health safe for safekeeping. | also understand that | must inform a nurse if | bring any electrical equipment to UofL Health (e.g., home insulin pumps; BiPAP machine, CPAP machine) and adhere to UofL Health policies regarding its use. | assume full responsibility for such electrical equipment and for any injury caused by the use of the electrical equipment brought from home.

COMMUNICATIONS

By providing my cell, landline, or any other phone number(s), | expressly consent to receiving communications from UofL Health, its staff, its contractors, collection agents, and others, at any numbers | provide or that are later acquired for me. These parties may use this information to contact me by live agent, voice mail, text message, using an auto dialer or other computer assisted technology, pre-recorded message(s), or by any other form of electronic communication for any purpose including, but not limited to, appointment and follow-up health care reminders, scheduling, my account(s), assignment of benefits, and/or financial responsibility. | understand that depending on my phone plan | could be charged for these calls or text messages. | agree to provide new number(s) if my number(s) change(s). Providing these numbers is not a condition of receiving healthcare services.
